  - [19:13:09 - 19:16:34] **Introduction to K-modes Clustering**

    Let's return to the lecture. We have discussed K-means, but now let's look at a variant of it called K-modes. This version is designed to handle categorical data. Remember, if your dataset contains non-numerical data—like the financial dataset we saw with investment types—you cannot run the standard K-means algorithm on it. A common principle in machine learning is to convert these into numerical values, but you don't actually have to do that. The K-modes algorithm applies the Hamming distance to this non-numerical dataset. It is essentially K-means but adapted with Hamming distance. There are only two main differences. First, in K-means, you can initialize by selecting any arbitrary point as a centroid. In K-modes, you must choose actual data points from the dataset as the initial centers. Second, when you update the centroid—which we call the "mode" here—the arithmetic mean is not meaningful for categorical data. Instead, we choose the most frequent value (majority vote) for each attribute. Other than these, the steps are exactly the same.

    我们回到讲座。我们已经讨论了 K-均值（K-means），现在我们来看它的一个变体，叫做 K-众数（K-modes）。这个版本是专门用来处理分类数据的。记得吗，如果你的数据集包含非数值数据——比如我们看到的包含投资类型的金融数据集——你是无法在上面运行标准的 K-means 算法的。机器学习中的一个常见原则是将这些数据转换为数值，但实际上你不需要通过这种方式。K-modes 算法基本上是将汉明距离（Hamming distance）应用于非数值数据集。它本质上就是使用了汉明距离的 K-means。主要区别只有两点。第一，在 K-means 中，你可以通过选择任意点来初始化质心；而在 K-modes 中，你必须从数据集中选择实际的数据点作为初始中心。第二，当你更新质心——在这里我们称之为“众数（mode）”——时，算术平均值对分类数据没有意义。相反，我们为每个属性选择出现频率最高的值（多数投票）。除了这两点，其他步骤完全相同。

  - [19:16:35 - 19:22:14] **K-modes Step 1: Assignment Phase**

    Let's look at an example. Suppose we want to obtain a two-cluster result (`K=2`) on a dataset containing investment information. We choose the first sample and the second sample as our initial modes. For Mode A (Sample 1), the features are "Stocks, High, Long-term." For Mode B (Sample 2), the features are "Bonds, Low, Short-term." Now, we calculate the Hamming distance from the other points to these two modes. Take the third sample, which is "Mutual Funds, Medium, Medium-term." The distance to Mode A is 3. Why 3? Because "Mutual Funds" is different from "Stocks," "Medium" risk is different from "High" risk, and "Medium-term" duration is different from "Long-term." All three attributes differ. Now compare the fourth sample to Mode A. We might find a distance of 1 because two attributes match and only one differs. We calculate these distances for all points. Then, we assign each point to the cluster with the closest mode. For instance, Sample 4 has a distance of 1 to Mode A and a distance of 3 to Mode B, so it goes to Cluster A. We do have a troublesome case with Sample 3, where the distance to both modes might be equal (a tie). In categorical clustering, ties happen quite often. In such cases, we just assign it arbitrarily to one cluster.

    让我们看一个例子。假设我们想在一个包含投资信息的数据集上得到两个聚类（`K=2`）。我们选择第一个样本和第二个样本作为初始众数。对于众数 A（样本 1），特征是“股票、高风险、长期”。对于众数 B（样本 2），特征是“债券、低风险、短期”。现在，我们计算其他点到这两个众数的汉明距离。以第三个样本为例，它是“共同基金、中等风险、中期”。它到众数 A 的距离是 3。为什么是 3？因为“共同基金”不同于“股票”，“中等”风险不同于“高”风险，“中期”不同于“长期”。三个属性都不同。现在比较第四个样本和众数 A，我们可能会发现距离是 1，因为有两个属性匹配，只有一个不同。我们计算所有点的距离。然后，我们将每个点分配给距离最近的众数所在的聚类。例如，样本 4 到众数 A 的距离是 1，到众数 B 的距离是 3，所以它属于聚类 A。样本 3 确实有个麻烦的情况，它到两个众数的距离可能相等（平局）。在分类聚类中，平局经常发生。在这种情况下，我们就任意将它分配给其中一个聚类。

  - [19:22:15 - 19:24:47] **K-modes Step 2: Update Phase**

    After assignment, we need to update the modes. Suppose Cluster 1 contains samples 1, 4, and 5. For the first attribute, the values are "Stocks," "ETF," and "Stocks." We take the majority vote, so the new mode's value is "Stocks." For the second attribute, risk tolerance, we have "High," "High," and "Medium." The majority is "High." We do this for all attributes. This is how we calculate the new mode for the first cluster. Similarly, we calculate the new mode for the second cluster using majority rule on its members: "Bonds, Low, Medium-term." If we reassign the points based on these new modes and the results don't change, the clustering is stable. The K-modes diagram looks essentially the same as K-means, but it uses a different metric and update rule. It is very useful in the business and financial world where data is often categorical. Since Hamming distance is easy to calculate, it is quite efficient.

    分配完成后，我们需要更新众数。假设聚类 1 包含样本 1、4 和 5。对于第一个属性，值分别是“股票”、“ETF”和“股票”。我们采取多数投票，所以新众数的值是“股票”。对于第二个属性，风险承受能力，我们有“高”、“高”和“中”。多数是“高”。我们对所有属性都这样做。这就是我们如何计算第一个聚类的新众数。同样，我们利用成员的多数规则计算第二个聚类的新众数：“债券、低、中期”。如果我们基于这些新众数重新分配点，且结果没有变化，那么聚类就是稳定的。K-modes 的图示看起来本质上和 K-means 一样，但它使用了不同的度量和更新规则。它在商业和金融领域非常有用，因为那里的数据通常是分类的。由于汉明距离很容易计算，所以它非常高效。

  - [19:24:48 - 19:27:47] **Introduction to Hierarchical Clustering**

    Now let's see another popular method: Hierarchical Clustering. This method takes a completely different approach. It outputs a set of nested clusters organized using a dendrogram. This is the tree-like structure you see here. A key advantage is that it doesn't require you to specify the number of clusters (`K`) in advance. It allows the analyst to examine various partitions of the data with different granularity before deciding which one to use. For example, if we have seven data points (x1 to x7), the dendrogram shows us how they group. A small branch connecting x6 and x7 implies a two-member cluster. A higher branch connecting x4 and x5 with the (x6, x7) group implies a larger cluster containing all four. As you go up the tree, the clusters get larger, eventually merging everything into one big cluster containing all points (x1 to x7).

    现在来看看另一种流行的方法：层次聚类（Hierarchical Clustering）。这种方法采用完全不同的路径。它输出一组嵌套的聚类，并使用树状图（dendrogram）进行组织。就是你们在这里看到的树状结构。一个关键优势是它不需要你预先指定聚类数量（`K`）。它允许分析师在决定使用哪种方案之前，以不同的粒度检查数据的各种划分。例如，如果我们有七个数据点（x1 到 x7），树状图展示了它们是如何分组的。连接 x6 和 x7 的小分支意味着一个包含两个成员的聚类。连接 x4 和 x5 与 (x6, x7) 组的更高分支意味着一个包含这四个点的更大聚类。当你沿着树向上看，聚类变得越来越大，最终将所有点（x1 到 x7）合并成一个包含所有点的大聚类。

  - [19:27:48 - 19:30:17] **Cutting the Dendrogram**

    So, how do you choose the final clusters? It is very flexible. You can "cut" the tree using a horizontal line. If you cut the dendrogram at a certain height, you might get a two-cluster result: one cluster with (x1, x2, x3) and another large cluster with (x4, x5, x6, x7). If you do another cut at a lower level, you might separate the second group, resulting in three clusters. This allows you to examine different solutions and choose the one that fits your application best. This is why it's called hierarchical—there are smaller clusters nested inside larger ones.

    那么，你如何选择最终的聚类呢？这非常灵活。你可以用一条水平线来“切割”这棵树。如果你在某个高度切割树状图，你可能会得到一个包含两个聚类的结果：一个聚类包含 (x1, x2, x3)，另一个大聚类包含 (x4, x5, x6, x7)。如果你在更低的位置切割，你可能会把第二组分开，从而得到三个聚类。这允许你检查不同的解决方案，并选择最适合你应用的一个。这就是为什么它被称为层次聚类——较小的聚类嵌套在较大的聚类中。

  - [19:30:18 - 19:36:53] **Agglomerative Clustering Strategy**

    The algorithm typically works in a "bottom-up" manner. In the very beginning, each data point is considered a single-point cluster. If you have 11 points, you start with 11 small clusters. Then, you merge the two closest clusters into a larger one. You look at the data, find the closest pair, and merge them. Then you look for the next closest pair—maybe two other points, or maybe a point and the cluster you just formed—and merge them. Each step reduces the number of clusters by one. You repeat this process, layer by layer, until eventually, all clusters are merged into a single large cluster. The dendrogram records this history. A connection between two branches represents a merge. For example, if two yellow points merge first, you get a small arch. If that group later merges with a blue group, you get a higher arch connecting them. The structure of the tree represents the containment relations of the clusters.

    该算法通常以“自底向上”的方式工作。最开始，每个数据点都被视为一个单点聚类。如果你有 11 个点，你就从 11 个小聚类开始。然后，你将两个最近的聚类合并成一个更大的聚类。你观察数据，找到最近的一对并合并它们。然后你寻找下一对最近的——可能是另外两个点，也可能是一个点和你刚刚形成的聚类——并将它们合并。每一步都会将聚类数量减少一个。你一层一层地重复这个过程，直到最终所有聚类合并成一个包含所有点的大聚类。树状图记录了这个历史。两个分支之间的连接代表一次合并。例如，如果两个黄色的点首先合并，你会得到一个小拱形。如果那一组后来与一组蓝色的点合并，你会得到一个连接它们的更高的拱形。树的结构代表了聚类的包含关系。

  - [19:36:54 - 19:38:35] **Meaning of Vertical Height**

    The length of the vertical lines in the dendrogram is meaningful. It represents the height at which the merge occurs. This height quantifies the similarity or distance between the two clusters being merged. If the vertical line is short, it means the two clusters were very close (very similar) when they merged. If the vertical line is long, it means the two groups were far apart (very dissimilar) before they were forced to merge. So, the height indicates the dissimilarity.

    树状图中垂直线的长度是有意义的。它代表了合并发生的高度。这个高度量化了被合并的两个聚类之间的相似度或距离。如果垂直线很短，意味着这两个聚类在合并时非常接近（非常相似）。如果垂直线很长，意味着这两组在被迫合并之前相距很远（非常不相似）。所以，高度表示不相似度。

  - [19:38:36 - 19:44:29] **Linkage Methods**

    We know how to calculate the distance between points (Euclidean, Manhattan), but how do we calculate the distance between *clusters*? This is called "Linkage," and there are four main ways to define it:

    1. **Single Linkage:** The minimum distance between any point in one cluster and any point in the other. It uses the closest pair of points.

    2. **Complete Linkage:** The maximum distance. It uses the furthest pair of points between the two clusters.

    3. **Average Linkage:** The mean distance. You calculate all possible pairwise distances between the points in Cluster A and Cluster B, sum them up, and divide by the total number of pairs. For a 3-point cluster and a 2-point cluster, you compute 6 distances and average them.

    4. **Centroid Linkage:** The distance between the centroids of the two clusters.

       Different linkage methods produce different results. In the example I showed, different linkages revealed different gene clusters. It's hard to say which is "best"; it depends on your application. In biology, one method might reveal an informative subtype while another reveals a different but equally valid pattern.

    我们知道如何计算点之间的距离（欧几里得、曼哈顿），但我们如何计算*聚类*之间的距离呢？这被称为“链接（Linkage）”，主要有四种定义方式：

    1. **单链接（Single Linkage）：** 一个聚类中的任意点与另一个聚类中的任意点之间的最小距离。它使用最近的一对点。

    2. **全链接（Complete Linkage）：** 最大距离。它使用两个聚类之间最远的一对点。

    3. **平均链接（Average Linkage）：** 平均距离。你计算聚类 A 和聚类 B 中所有点对之间的距离，将它们相加，然后除以点对的总数。对于一个 3 点聚类和一个 2 点聚类，你要计算 6 个距离并取平均。

    4. **质心链接（Centroid Linkage）：** 两个聚类质心之间的距离。

       不同的链接方法会产生不同的结果。在我展示的例子中，不同的链接揭示了不同的基因聚类。很难说哪个是“最好的”；这取决于你的应用。在生物学中，一种方法可能会揭示一种有信息的亚型，而另一种方法可能会揭示另一种同样有效的模式。

  - [19:44:30 - 19:47:56] **Example Calculation and The Cutting Rule**

    Let's look at a 1D example to clarify the height. Suppose we have points on a line. We merge them step by step. If we use average linkage, the height of the connection represents the average distance between the points in the left branch and the right branch. In the diagram, a height of 6.416 is the average distance between the points in Cluster A and Cluster B.

    A student asked: "When you say choose the longest vertical line to cut, which line would that be?"

    In this scenario, if you look at the dendrogram, there is a very long vertical line before the final merge. Cutting across this longest line separates the two most dissimilar groups, giving you a stable two-cluster solution. If you want three clusters, you would look for the next longest vertical gap and cut there. The rule of thumb is to cut where the vertical gap is largest, as this implies a large jump in dissimilarity.

    让我们看一个一维的例子来阐明高度的含义。假设我们在一条直线上有点。我们要一步步合并它们。如果我们使用平均链接，连接的高度代表左分支和右分支中点之间的平均距离。在图中，6.416 的高度是聚类 A 和聚类 B 中点之间的平均距离。

    有学生问：“当你说选择最长的垂直线进行切割时，是指哪一条线？”

    在这种情况下，如果你看树状图，在最后一次合并之前有一条非常长的垂直线。切断这条最长的线会将两个最不相似的组分开，从而给你一个稳定的双聚类解。如果你想要三个聚类，你会寻找下一个最长的垂直间隙并在那里切割。经验法则是垂直间隙最大的地方切割，因为这意味着不相似度有一个大的跳跃。

  - [19:47:57 - 19:52:14] **Pros and Cons of Hierarchical Clustering**

    **Summary of Pros and Cons:**

    - **Pros:** You don't need to predefine the number of clusters, unlike K-means. The tree structure provides excellent visualization and insight into the data structure. It works with any distance metric.
    - **Cons:** It is computationally expensive for large datasets. K-means is linear, but Hierarchical Clustering requires calculating pairwise distances. If you have 1 million data points, you need to calculate 1 million times 1 million distances (10^12), which is infeasible. K-means might only require calculating distances to 3 centroids for each point (3 million calculations). So, hierarchical is not suitable for massive data. It is also sensitive to noise and outliers. Furthermore, once clusters are merged, the change cannot be undone. If a mistake is made early (merging two points that shouldn't be together), it propagates to the end.

    **优缺点总结：**

    - **优点：** 与 K-means 不同，你不需要预先定义聚类数量。树状结构提供了极佳的可视化效果，让你能深入了解数据结构。它适用于任何距离度量。
    - **缺点：** 对于大数据集，计算成本很高。K-means 是线性的，但层次聚类需要计算成对距离。如果你有 100 万个数据点，你需要计算 100 万乘以 100 万次距离（10^12），这是不可行的。而 K-means 可能只需要计算每个点到 3 个质心的距离（300 万次计算）。所以，层次聚类不适合海量数据。它对噪声和异常值也很敏感。此外，一旦聚类合并，更改就无法撤销。如果在早期犯了错误（合并了两个不应该在一起的点），这个错误会一直延续到最后。

  - [19:52:15 - 19:58:29] **Application: Breast Cancer Subtyping**

    Finally, a real-world application: subtyping breast cancer. Breast cancer is a complex disease caused by gene mutations. Traditionally, we classify it using hormone proteins:

    - **ER+ / PR+:** The cancer expresses Estrogen or Progesterone receptors. These are treatable with hormone therapies.

    - **HER2+:** The cancer has high expression of the HER2 protein. This is aggressive but we have specific inhibitors (drugs) to control it.

    - **Triple-negative:** This is the most troublesome type. It is ER-, PR-, and HER2-. It lacks targets for standard therapies and has a high death rate.

      About 20 years ago, researchers used DNA sequences and gene expression data (1,752 genes across 84 samples) to reclassify breast cancer. They applied hierarchical clustering to this genetic data. The result revealed "intrinsic" molecular subtypes (like Luminal A, Luminal B, Basal-like, etc.) which overlap with the clinical types but provide better understanding and potentially new treatment targets. This is a classic example of how hierarchical clustering is used in medicine.

      That's all for today. If you need to take the makeup quiz, please stay; others may leave.

    最后，讲一个现实世界的应用：乳腺癌亚型分类。乳腺癌是由基因突变引起的复杂疾病。传统上，我们使用激素蛋白对其进行分类：

    - **ER+ / PR+：** 癌症表达雌激素或孕激素受体。这些可以通过激素疗法治疗。

    - **HER2+：** 癌症具有 HER2 蛋白的高表达。这具有侵略性，但我们有特定的抑制剂（药物）来控制它。

    - **三阴性（Triple-negative）：** 这是最麻烦的类型。它是 ER-、PR- 和 HER2-。它缺乏标准疗法的靶点，死亡率很高。

      大约 20 年前，研究人员利用 DNA 序列和基因表达数据（84 个样本中的 1,752 个基因）重新分类乳腺癌。他们将层次聚类应用于这些遗传数据。结果揭示了“固有”分子亚型（如 Luminal A、Luminal B、基底样型等），这些亚型与临床类型重叠，但提供了更好的理解和潜在的新治疗靶点。这是层次聚类在医学中应用的经典案例。

      今天就讲到这里。如果你需要参加补考，请留下；其他人可以离开了。
## Week 7 Lecture 6
  - [19:05:11 - 19:07:18] **Introduction and Recap of Unsupervised Learning**

    Good evening, everyone. Let's get started with the lecture. Can you all hear me? Okay, good. If you have any questions throughout the class, please feel free to type them into the chat box. Tonight, we are going to continue our discussion on unsupervised learning. As a recap, the primary goal of unsupervised learning is to discover underlying patterns and find groups of similar samples within an unlabeled dataset. We are exclusively dealing with data that has no labels. Some of the most popular types of unsupervised learning algorithms include clustering techniques, such as K-Means and Hierarchical clustering. Today, I will introduce another clustering method called DBSCAN, which is a very intuitive algorithm. After that, we will shift our focus to popular dimensionality reduction methods, specifically looking at Principal Component Analysis (PCA), t-SNE, and UMAP. I will primarily focus on PCA and t-SNE for this session. That is our roadmap for today.

    大家晚上好，我们准备开始上课。都能听见我说话吗？好的，没问题。如果大家在听课过程中有任何问题，请随时在聊天框里提问。今晚我们将继续讨论无监督学习。回顾一下，无监督学习的主要目标是在无标签的数据集中发现潜在的模式，并找出相似样本的集合。我们处理的全都是没有标签的数据。目前最流行的一些无监督学习算法包括聚类技术，比如 K-Means 和层次聚类。今天，我将介绍另一种名为 DBSCAN 的聚类方法，这是一种非常直观的算法。之后，我们将把重点转向流行的降维方法，具体包括主成分分析 (PCA)、t-SNE 和 UMAP。在这节课中，我将主要聚焦于 PCA 和 t-SNE。这就是我们今天的学习计划。

  - [19:07:18 - 19:10:09] **Introduction to DBSCAN and its Hyperparameters**

    Let's walk through the DBSCAN algorithm first. The core idea is actually quite simple: clusters are defined as dense regions of points that are separated by low-density regions. This is fundamentally different from K-Means. In K-Means, clusters are defined by their central points, or centroids. But in DBSCAN, a cluster is defined purely by the density of the points in a given region. The major advantage of this density-based method is that it can detect clusters of completely arbitrary shapes, unlike K-Means which tends to force spherical clusters. To make this work, the algorithm relies on two critical hyperparameters. The first is epsilon, which defines the radius of our neighborhood. Basically, we use epsilon to determine the size of a point's neighborhood. If the distance between point A and point B is less than or equal to epsilon, we say they are epsilon-neighbors. You can visualize this by drawing a circle with a radius of epsilon around a point, and any point falling inside that circle is considered a neighbor. For instance, if you look at a dark point on a graph, it might have multiple epsilon-neighbors surrounding it. The second hyperparameter is M, which is the minimum number of points required within that epsilon radius to officially form a dense region. M gives us a quantitative bound to define what "dense" actually means for our specific dataset.

    让我们先来看看 DBSCAN 算法。它的核心思想其实很简单：聚类被定义为由低密度区域分隔开的点的稠密区域。这与 K-Means 有着本质的区别。在 K-Means 中，聚类是由它们的中心点（或质心）来定义的。但在 DBSCAN 中，聚类完全是由给定区域内点的密度来定义的。这种基于密度的方法的最大优势在于，它可以检测出完全任意形状的聚类，而不像 K-Means 那样倾向于划分出球形聚类。为了实现这一点，该算法依赖于两个关键的超参数。第一个是 epsilon (邻域半径)，它定义了我们邻域的范围。基本上，我们使用 epsilon 来确定一个点的邻域大小。如果点 A 和点 B 之间的距离小于或等于 epsilon，我们就说它们是 epsilon 邻居。你可以这样想象：围绕一个点画一个半径为 epsilon 的圆，任何落在这个圆内的点都被视为邻居。例如，如果你看图上的一个黑点，它的周围可能有多个 epsilon 邻居。第二个超参数是 M，即在 epsilon 半径内正式形成一个稠密区域所需的最小点数。M 为我们提供了一个定量的边界，用来定义在我们的特定数据集中“稠密”到底意味着什么。

  - [19:10:09 - 19:12:36] **Defining Core Points, Border Points, and Outliers**

    Using these two parameters, epsilon and M, we can categorize every data point into one of three distinct types. The first type is the "core point." A core point is any point that has at least M epsilon-neighbors within its radius. In our visual illustrations, these are usually marked in red—they represent the heart of a dense region. The second type is the "border point." A border point is not dense enough to be a core point itself (meaning it has fewer than M neighbors), but it is located within the epsilon distance of at least one valid core point. In other words, it sits right on the edge or boundary of a dense cluster. The last type of point is the "outlier," sometimes called noise. An outlier is a point that is neither a core point nor falls within the epsilon distance of any core point. It is completely isolated from the dense regions. For example, a blue point situated far away from all the other point clusters would be classified as an outlier. So, fundamentally, we are just using spatial distance and neighbor counts to clearly categorize every point as a core point, a border point, or an outlier. Is that concept clear to everyone?

    利用 epsilon 和 M 这两个参数，我们可以将每个数据点归类为三种截然不同的类型之一。第一种类型是“核心点 (Core Point)”。核心点是指在其半径内至少有 M 个 epsilon 邻居的点。在我们的图例中，这些点通常标为红色——它们代表了稠密区域的中心。第二种类型是“边界点 (Border Point)”。边界点本身的密度不足以成为核心点（意味着它的邻居少于 M 个），但它位于至少一个有效核心点的 epsilon 距离之内。换句话说，它刚好位于密集聚类的边缘或边界上。最后一种点是“离群点 (Outlier)”，有时也叫噪声。离群点既不是核心点，也不在任何核心点的 epsilon 距离内。它完全孤立于稠密区域之外。例如，一个远离所有其他点群的蓝色点就会被归类为离群点。所以，从根本上讲，我们只是使用空间距离和邻居数量，清晰地将每个点分类为核心点、边界点或离群点。这个概念大家都清楚吗？

  - [19:12:36 - 19:16:45] **DBSCAN Algorithm Step 1 & Student Q&A on Epsilon**

    Now let's look at the actual step-by-step DBSCAN algorithm using a simple toy dataset mapped on a 2D grid. Because it's on a standard square grid, the distance between any two adjacent points horizontally or vertically is exactly 1. However, the diagonal distance between points is the square root of 2, which is approximately 1.4142. Step one of the algorithm is to build an epsilon-neighbor graph. We do this by connecting two points with an edge if the distance between them is less than our chosen epsilon. A student, Christina, just asked in the chat: "How do we know to set epsilon to 1.45?" That is a great question. Epsilon is a hyperparameter, meaning it's a value we must set before running the analysis. I intentionally set epsilon to 1.45 for this specific grid example because I want points that are diagonally adjacent (which have a distance of 1.4142) to be counted as neighbors. Since 1.4142 is less than 1.45, the algorithm will draw a line connecting them. If I had set epsilon to 1.0, diagonal points wouldn't connect. So setting it to 1.45 is just a pedagogical choice to illustrate how the connections form on this grid. Once we have our epsilon, we simply build the graph by drawing edges between all points that fall within that threshold distance.

    现在让我们使用一个映射在 2D 网格上的简单玩具数据集，来逐步看看 DBSCAN 算法的实际运行过程。因为它在一个标准的方形网格上，所以水平或垂直相邻的任意两点之间的距离恰好是 1。然而，点与点之间的对角线距离是 2 的平方根，大约是 1.4142。该算法的第一步是构建一个 epsilon 邻域图。如果两点之间的距离小于我们选定的 epsilon，我们就用一条边把它们连接起来。有位同学，Christina，刚才在聊天区问：“我们怎么知道要把 epsilon 设置为 1.45？”这是个很好的问题。Epsilon 是一个超参数，意思是这是我们在运行分析之前必须设定的一个值。我特意为这个网格示例将 epsilon 设置为 1.45，是因为我希望对角线相邻的点（它们的距离是 1.4142）也能被算作邻居。因为 1.4142 小于 1.45，所以算法会画一条线将它们连接起来。如果我把 epsilon 设为 1.0，对角线上的点就不会连接了。所以把它设为 1.45 只是一个教学上的选择，为了演示在这个网格上连接是如何形成的。一旦我们确定了 epsilon，我们只需在所有落在该阈值距离内的点之间画上连线，就可以构建出这个图。

  - [19:16:45 - 19:22:41] **DBSCAN Algorithm Step 2 & Student Q&A on Neighborhood Cutoffs**

    Moving to step two: we need to identify which points are core, border, or outliers. We do this simply by counting how many edges (or neighbors) each point has. For example, if a point has two lines connecting it to others, it has two close neighbors. If a point has six lines, it has six neighbors. In our example, we have set the hyperparameter M to 3. This means any point with 3 or more connections is designated as a core point, which we color red. Now, Shonor and KB pointed out in the chat that one of the points on the slide seems to have 4 neighbors instead of 3, and might be missing a red line. Thank you for noticing that! Yes, it appears there is a missing line in the graphic. If we draw that missing edge, that point effectively has 4 neighbors. But remember, M equals 3 is just the minimum cutoff. Whether it has 3, 4, or 6 neighbors, as long as it meets that minimum threshold of 3, it is successfully classified as a red core point. If a point has only 2 neighbors, it fails to be a core point. But if one of those 2 neighbors happens to be a red core point, it gets classified as a border point. If it has no connections or isn't near any core points, it remains an isolated outlier. So, we rely entirely on these edge counts to categorize everything.

    进入第二步：我们需要识别哪些点是核心点、边界点或离群点。我们只需简单地计算每个点有多少条边（或邻居）就可以做到这一点。例如，如果一个点有两条线连接到其他点，它就有两个近邻。如果一个点有六条线，它就有六个邻居。在我们的例子中，我们将超参数 M 设置为 3。这意味着任何有 3 个或更多连接的点都被指定为核心点，我们将其涂成红色。刚才，Shonor 和 KB 在聊天区指出，幻灯片上的一个点似乎有 4 个邻居而不是 3 个，并且可能漏画了一条红线。谢谢你们的提醒！是的，图表上似乎确实漏画了一条线。如果我们补上那条缺失的边，那个点实际上就有 4 个邻居。但请记住，M 等于 3 只是最低的截断阈值。无论它有 3 个、4 个还是 6 个邻居，只要它达到了 3 这个最低阈值，它就会被成功归类为红色的核心点。如果一个点只有 2 个邻居，它就不能成为核心点。但如果这 2 个邻居中恰好有一个是红色的核心点，它就会被归类为边界点。如果它没有任何连接，或者附近没有任何核心点，它就仍然是一个孤立的离群点。因此，我们完全依赖这些边的计数来对所有点进行分类。

  - [19:22:41 - 19:24:36] **DBSCAN Algorithm Step 3: Forming Clusters**

    Step three is where we finally form the actual clusters. The rule here is that connected core points merge to form a single cluster. Specifically, two core points belong to the same cluster if you can trace a path between them consisting entirely of other core points. Looking at our diagram, if you pick a core point at the top and can follow a trail of connected red dots all the way to a core point at the bottom, they all belong to one massive cluster. Similarly, if you have a separate group of six core points connected exclusively to each other on the other side of the graph, those six form their own distinct second cluster. Once the core networks are established, we then look at the border points.

    第三步是我们最终形成实际聚类的地方。这里的规则是，相连的核心点合并形成一个单一的聚类。具体来说，如果你能在两个核心点之间追踪到一条完全由其他核心点组成的路径，那么这两个核心点就属于同一个聚类。看看我们的图表，如果你在顶部选择一个核心点，并且能顺着一条相连的红点轨迹一直走到下方的一个核心点，那么它们就都属于一个庞大的聚类。同样地，如果在图的另一侧有另外六个核心点仅彼此相连，那么这六个点就形成了它们自己独立的第二个聚类。一旦核心网络建立起来，我们接着就会来处理边界点。

  - [19:24:36 - 19:30:19] **Technical Difficulties**

    (The professor experiences several minutes of technical difficulties attempting to flip the slides and operate the drawing tool on the presentation software, resulting in a brief pause in the lecture content.)

    （教授在尝试翻页和操作演示软件上的绘图工具时遇到了一些技术故障，导致课程内容短暂亦停了几分钟。）

  - [19:30:19 - 19:32:05] **Assigning Border Points & Student Q&A on Cluster Boundaries**

    Alright, now that the clusters are formed by the core points, we must assign each border point to a cluster. A border point is assigned to a cluster if that cluster contains at least one of the border point's close neighbors. We had a question in the chat about a specific orange dot: "Is it a core point or a border point?" Because I added that extra edge earlier, it met the threshold, so it is indeed a core point. Another excellent question just came in: "Can the light green dots in the middle be assigned to the red cluster instead?" Yes, absolutely! This happens when a border point sits directly between two different clusters and has core neighbors in both the green and the red clusters. The algorithm's rule is that a border point can only be assigned to one single cluster. However, it is essentially arbitrary which one it gets assigned to; the algorithm will just pick one of the valid neighboring clusters. It doesn't matter mathematically which one it joins, as long as it gets assigned. Ultimately, all border points get absorbed into a cluster, while the outliers remain totally unassigned. There is no cluster for outliers. That completes the three simple steps of the DBSCAN algorithm. Are there any questions?

    好了，现在既然核心点已经形成了聚类，我们必须将每个边界点分配给一个聚类。如果一个聚类包含边界点的至少一个近邻，那么该边界点就会被分配给这个聚类。聊天区里有个关于某个特定橙色点的问题：“它究竟是核心点还是边界点？”因为我之前加了那条额外的边，它达到了阈值，所以它确实是一个核心点。刚才还有一个非常好的问题：“中间的浅绿色点可以被分配给红色聚类吗？”是的，绝对可以！当一个边界点正好位于两个不同的聚类之间，并且在绿色和红色聚类中都有核心邻居时，就会出现这种情况。算法的规则是一个边界点只能被分配给一个聚类。然而，它究竟被分配给哪一个本质上是任意的；算法只会挑选其中一个有效的相邻聚类。从数学上讲，它加入哪一个都无所谓，只要它被分配了就行。最终，所有的边界点都会被吸收到聚类中，而离群点则完全不被分配。离群点不属于任何聚类。这就完成了 DBSCAN 算法的三个简单步骤。大家有什么问题吗？

  - [19:32:05 - 19:38:57] **Pros, Cons, and Visualization of DBSCAN**

    To summarize DBSCAN, clusters naturally grow through connected dense regions, while isolated points are naturally left behind as noise. The pros of this method are fantastic: you don't need to specify the number of clusters beforehand (unlike specifying 'K' in K-Means), it effortlessly handles arbitrary cluster shapes, and it automatically identifies outliers for you without any extra work. I highly recommend checking out the Naftali Harris blog linked in the slides; it has a great interactive visualization where you can set epsilon to 1 and M to 4, and watch the clusters organically expand point by point. However, DBSCAN does have cons. The biggest weakness is its extreme sensitivity to its hyperparameters, epsilon and M. If you look at the visualization on the slide, setting M to 4 perfectly identifies four distinct clusters. But if you change M to 5, increasing the density requirement just slightly, it suddenly splits a large, cohesive cluster right down the middle, resulting in five clusters. This hyper-sensitivity means that if you don't tune epsilon and M perfectly, your results can change drastically.

    总结一下 DBSCAN，聚类是通过相连的稠密区域自然生长的，而孤立的点则自然被作为噪声丢弃。这种方法的优点非常棒：你不需要预先指定聚类的数量（不像在 K-Means 中需要指定‘K’），它能毫不费力地处理任意形状的聚类，而且它会自动为你识别出离群点，不需要任何额外的工作。我强烈建议大家去看看幻灯片里链接的 Naftali Harris 博客；那里有一个非常棒的交互式可视化工具，你可以把 epsilon 设为 1，M 设为 4，然后观察聚类是如何逐个点有机扩展的。然而，DBSCAN 也有缺点。最大的弱点是它对超参数 epsilon 和 M 极端敏感。如果你看幻灯片上的可视化图，将 M 设为 4 可以完美地识别出四个不同的聚类。但如果你把 M 改为 5，仅仅稍微提高了密度要求，它突然就会把一个原本紧密结合的大聚类从中间劈开，导致出现五个聚类。这种超高的敏感度意味着，如果你不能完美地调整 epsilon 和 M，你的结果可能会发生巨大的改变。

  - [19:38:57 - 19:45:27] **Motivation for Dimensionality Reduction and PCA**

    Now, let's move on to our next major topic: Principal Component Analysis, or PCA, which is a powerful dimensionality reduction algorithm. Why do we care about dimensionality reduction? Primarily for visualization. Visualization is an incredibly important communication tool. Humans are biologically optimized for visual pattern recognition. Patterns that are nearly impossible to detect when looking at raw numerical tables become instantly obvious when visualized. A famous example of this is a concept from a textbook by Edward Tufte, showcasing four datasets that have identical summary statistics—same mean, same variance. If you just look at the raw numbers in the table, you cannot tell them apart. But if you plot them in 2D, you instantly see one is a random scatter, one is a clean quadratic curve, one is a straight line, and one is just a line with a massive outlier. Visualizing data reveals non-linear patterns, group separations, and outliers immediately. But here is the catch: we can realistically only interpret 2D plots. Even 3D plots are terribly flawed. Consider a 3D bar chart: it is incredibly difficult to accurately estimate the height or volume of the bars due to perspective. We are generally okay at estimating linear distance (1D), but estimating area (squared radius) or volume (cubic radius) is cognitively difficult. If I give you a height of 3.4, you might intuitively grasp it, but you likely cannot easily compute or visualize the square or cube of 3.4 in your head. Because humans struggle to interpret 3D graphics, we desperately need methods to map high-dimensional data down into a flat, 2D space so we can actually plot and understand it.

    现在，让我们进入下一个主要话题：主成分分析，简称 PCA，这是一种强大的降维算法。我们为什么要在意降维呢？主要是为了数据可视化。可视化是一种极其重要的沟通工具。人类在生物学上天生就擅长视觉模式识别。那些在查看原始数字表格时几乎不可能被发现的模式，一旦被可视化，就会立刻变得显而易见。关于这一点，Edward Tufte 教科书中的一个著名例子就展示了四个数据集，它们具有完全相同的汇总统计数据——相同的均值，相同的方差。如果你只看表格里的原始数字，你根本无法区分它们。但如果你把它们在二维平面上画出来，你会立刻看到一个是随机散布的点，一个是清晰的二次曲线，一个是直线，还有一个是带有一个巨大离群点的直线。可视化数据能立即揭示非线性模式、群体分离和离群点。但问题在于：在现实中，我们只能解读 2D（二维）图表。即便是 3D（三维）图表也存在极大的缺陷。想想 3D 柱状图：由于透视的原因，想要准确估计柱子的高度或体积是极其困难的。我们通常比较擅长估计线性距离（1D），但在认知上很难估计面积（半径的平方）或体积（半径的立方）。如果我给你一个 3.4 的高度，你可能会凭直觉理解它，但你可能很难在脑海中轻松计算或想象出 3.4 的平方或立方。因为人类很难解读 3D 图形，我们迫切需要将高维数据映射到扁平的 2D 空间中，这样我们才能真正地绘制并理解它。

  - [19:45:27 - 19:52:49] **Compressing Correlated Features with Linear Mapping**

    Beyond just visualization, dimensionality reduction is vital for improving machine learning models, especially classifications. In high-dimensional spaces, data suffers from the "curse of dimensionality"—the data points become incredibly sparse. Because points are spread so far apart, standard distance metrics lose their meaning. Almost every pair of points appears to be roughly the same distance apart, which cripples distance-based algorithms. Reducing dimensions improves the generalization of learning models by compressing highly correlated features into a smaller set of entirely new features, which we call principal components. PCA uses a linear function to achieve this, aiming to retain as much of the original variance—or information—as possible. Let's look at a toy example to see how this linear mapping works. Suppose we have a dataset with four features: x1, x2, x3, and x4. We can create a brand new feature, let's call it y, by assigning weights to the original features. Our linear function might be y = x1 + 2x2 + x3 + 5x4. So, for a sample row where the values are 12, 15, 18, and 0.40, we calculate the new y value as 12 plus (2 times 15) plus 18 plus (5 times 0.40). That equals 12 + 30 + 18 + 2, giving us a final value of 62. By doing this across all rows, we compress four dimensions into a single new feature value. In statistical terms, this linear mapping is just matrix multiplication. We take our data matrix and multiply it by a weight vector—in this case, [1, 2, 1, 5]—to output a new, single-column vector containing values like 62, 57.5, and so on.

    除了可视化之外，降维对于改进机器学习模型（特别是分类模型）也至关重要。在高维空间中，数据会遭受“维度灾难”——数据点变得极其稀疏。因为点与点之间散布得太开，标准的距离度量标准就失去了意义。几乎每一对点之间的距离看起来都差不多，这会让基于距离的算法失效。降维通过将高度相关的特征压缩成一组全新的、数量更少的特征（我们称之为主成分），来提高学习模型的泛化能力。PCA 使用线性函数来实现这一点，旨在尽可能多地保留原始方差（即信息）。让我们看一个玩具示例，看看这种线性映射是如何工作的。假设我们有一个包含四个特征的数据集：x1、x2、x3 和 x4。我们可以通过给原始特征分配权重来创建一个全新的特征，我们称之为 y。我们的线性函数可能是 y = x1 + 2x2 + x3 + 5x4。那么，对于值为 12、15、18 和 0.40 的样本行，我们将新的 y 值计算为 12 加上（2 乘以 15）加上 18 加上（5 乘以 0.40）。这等于 12 + 30 + 18 + 2，最后得出的值为 62。通过对所有行进行这种计算，我们将四个维度压缩成了一个单一的全新特征值。用统计学术语来说，这种线性映射其实就是矩阵乘法。我们把数据矩阵乘以一个权重向量（在这个例子中是 [1, 2, 1, 5]），就会输出一个新的单列向量，里面包含诸如 62、57.5 这样的值。

  - [19:52:49 - 19:59:07] **Maximizing Variance in PCA**

    The critical question is: how do we choose the optimal weights? Which specific combination of 'a' and 'b' will maximize the information retained in our new feature? In statistics, 'information' is directly measured by variance. If we look at a 2D scatter plot with 5 points, and we choose a weight vector where a=1 and b=0, our linear combination is simply taking the x-axis value and ignoring the y-axis entirely. Our projected points would fall precisely on the x-axis. But if we choose a strange, slanted vector, our data points project onto a diagonal line defined by that vector, resulting in totally different values. Every distinct combination of 'a' and 'b' yields a different projection, and therefore, a different variance. To calculate this variance for the projected points, say their values are 2, 3, 4, 5, and 6, we first find the mean, which is 4. The variance is the sum of the squared differences from that mean: (2-4)^2 + (3-4)^2 + (4-4)^2 + (5-4)^2 + (6-4)^2. The ultimate goal of PCA is to systematically find the specific weight vector (the specific 'a' and 'b') that results in the absolute highest possible variance for those projected points.

    最关键的问题是：我们该如何选择最佳的权重？'a' 和 'b' 的哪种特定组合能最大化保留在新特征中的信息？在统计学中，“信息”是直接通过方差来衡量的。如果我们看一个包含 5 个点的 2D 散点图，我们选择一个权重向量，其中 a=1 且 b=0，我们的线性组合就只是单纯地提取 x 轴的值，而完全忽略 y 轴。我们投影的点将正好落在 x 轴上。但如果我们选择一个奇特的、倾斜的向量，我们的数据点就会投影到由该向量定义的对角线上，从而产生完全不同的值。'a' 和 'b' 的每一种不同组合都会产生不同的投影，因此也会产生不同的方差。为了计算这些投影点的方差，假设它们的值是 2、3、4、5 和 6，我们首先求出均值，即 4。方差就是各点与该均值之差的平方和：(2-4)^2 + (3-4)^2 + (4-4)^2 + (5-4)^2 + (6-4)^2。PCA 的最终目标是系统地找到特定的权重向量（特定的 'a' 和 'b'），使得这些投影点能获得绝对最高的方差。

  - [19:59:07 - 20:04:40] **Student Q&A on Projections and Column Vectors**

    We have a question from the archive asking, "How do you plot a column vector as a 1D point on a 2D graph?" This is a great conceptual question. The weight vector itself defines a 1-dimensional line passing through the 2D space. When we apply the transformation, we are drawing a perpendicular line from each original data point directly onto this vector line. The resulting projected point is plotted exactly at that intersection. For example, if our vector is a=3/5 and b=4/5, and our original point is (2, 1), the calculation is 2(3/5) + 1(4/5), which equals 6/5 + 4/5, summing to 10/5, which is exactly 2. That value of '2' represents the physical distance from the origin point (0,0) along our new diagonal 1D line. Another question asked, "Why are the projection lines perpendicular?" They are perpendicular because orthogonal projection mathematically guarantees the shortest distance from the original point to the line, which is how we accurately map its value into the lower-dimensional space. The main takeaway is that you are searching for the specific line (defined by the weight vector) where, once all points are perpendicularly dropped onto it, they are spread out as vastly as possible.

    我们在存档里看到一个问题：“你是如何在 2D 图表上将列向量绘制成 1D 点的？”这是一个很好的概念性问题。权重向量本身定义了一条穿过 2D 空间的 1 维直线。当我们应用转换时，我们是从每个原始数据点直接向这条向量线画一条垂直线。由此产生的投影点就精确地绘制在那个交点上。例如，如果我们的向量是 a=3/5 和 b=4/5，而我们的原始点是 (2, 1)，那么计算过程就是 2(3/5) + 1(4/5)，等于 6/5 + 4/5，总和为 10/5，结果恰好是 2。这个值“2”代表了沿着我们这条新的对角线 1D 直线，从原点 (0,0) 出发的物理距离。还有人问：“为什么投影线是垂直的？”它们是垂直的，是因为正交投影在数学上保证了从原始点到直线的最短距离，这正是我们准确地将其值映射到低维空间的方法。这里的主要结论是，你要寻找一条特定的直线（由权重向量定义），当所有的点都垂直落在这条直线上时，它们能尽可能广泛地分散开来。

  - [20:04:40 - 20:13:30] **Linear Algebra Foundations: Eigenvalues and Eigenvectors**

    Fortunately, finding this optimal line doesn't require guessing; the exact solution is found using linear algebra, specifically through eigenvalues and eigenvectors. Let me explain these concepts. Usually, when you multiply a matrix by a vector, it alters both the scale (length) and the direction of the vector in space. For example, if we have matrix A = [[2, 3], [4, 1]] and we multiply it by the point (2, -7), the result is a massive negative coordinate (-18) pointing in an entirely different direction. However, something magical happens if we multiply that same matrix A by the vector (2, 2). The calculation becomes: for the top row, 2(2) + 3(2) = 10, and for the bottom row, 4(2) + 1(2) = 10. The output is (10, 10). Notice that (10, 10) is exactly 5 times our original vector (2, 2). The vector did not change direction at all; it was purely scaled outward by a multiplier of 5. When a matrix transformation only scales a vector without changing its fundamental direction, we call that vector an "eigenvector" of the matrix, and the scaling multiplier (in this case, 5) is its "eigenvalue." Not every random square matrix has eigenvectors. But crucially, symmetric matrices are mathematically guaranteed to have a set of linearly independent eigenvectors. This unique property is the entire mathematical engine driving PCA.

    幸运的是，寻找这条最佳直线并不需要靠猜；我们可以使用线性代数，特别是通过特征值和特征向量来找到精确的解。让我解释一下这些概念。通常，当你把一个矩阵乘以一个向量时，它会同时改变该向量在空间中的尺度（长度）和方向。例如，如果我们有矩阵 A = [[2, 3], [4, 1]]，我们用它乘以点 (2, -7)，结果会是一个指向完全不同方向的庞大负坐标 (-18)。然而，如果我们用同一个矩阵 A 乘以向量 (2, 2)，奇妙的事情就会发生。计算变成：对于顶行，2(2) + 3(2) = 10，对于底行，4(2) + 1(2) = 10。输出结果是 (10, 10)。请注意，(10, 10) 刚好是我们原始向量 (2, 2) 的 5 倍。这个向量的方向根本没有改变；它纯粹只是向外缩放了 5 倍。当矩阵转换仅仅缩放了一个向量而没有改变其基本方向时，我们就称该向量为矩阵的“特征向量 (eigenvector)”，而那个缩放乘数（在这个例子中是 5）就是它的“特征值 (eigenvalue)”。并不是每一个随机的方阵都有特征向量。但至关重要的是，对称矩阵在数学上被保证拥有一组线性无关的特征向量。这个独特的性质正是驱动 PCA 的整个数学引擎。

  - [20:13:30 - 20:17:08] **Defining Principal Components**

    In PCA, we don't just use any matrix; we calculate the covariance matrix of our dataset. A covariance matrix is inherently symmetric, which guarantees we can extract its eigenvectors. These eigenvectors are what we call our "Principal Components." Once computed, we order these principal components in descending order based on their corresponding eigenvalues. The eigenvector with the absolute largest eigenvalue becomes our First Principal Component (PC1). Because its eigenvalue represents the amount of variance explained, PC1 physically represents the single direction through our high-dimensional data that captures the maximum possible variance. It is the single most informative line we can draw. The second eigenvector becomes PC2, capturing the second highest variance, perfectly orthogonal to the first, and so on. These ordered eigenvectors effectively define a brand new coordinate system optimized purely for representing the variance in our data.

    在 PCA 中，我们不仅仅使用任何矩阵；我们会计算数据集的协方差矩阵。协方差矩阵天生就是对称的，这就保证了我们能够提取出它的特征向量。这些特征向量就是我们所说的“主成分 (Principal Components)”。计算出来后，我们根据它们相应的特征值按降序对这些主成分进行排序。拥有绝对最大特征值的特征向量成为我们的第一主成分 (PC1)。因为它的特征值代表了解释的方差量，PC1 在物理上代表了穿过我们高维数据、能够捕获最大可能方差的单一方向。这是我们能画出的包含信息量最大的一条直线。第二个特征向量成为 PC2，它捕获第二高的方差，且与第一个完全正交，以此类推。这些经过排序的特征向量有效地定义了一个全新的坐标系，该坐标系纯粹是为了优化表示我们数据中的方差而建立的。

  - [20:17:08 - 20:21:44] **The PCA Algorithm and Practical Applications**

    To put this all together, PCA is a tool that takes highly correlated, linearly related features and compresses them into a few main, completely uncorrelated components. A stellar application of this is in genomics. If you have a gene expression dataset containing hundreds of patients and thousands of individual genes acting as features, you can't plot 10,000 dimensions. But by running PCA, you can map those thousands of dimensions down to just PC1 and PC2. When you plot those two dimensions, you might clearly see patients grouping based on cancer types, like fibroadenoma separating beautifully from metastatic adenocarcinoma, purely based on the variance captured by those top two components. The algorithmic steps to achieve this are straightforward: Step 1, center the data matrix by subtracting the mean of each feature, effectively normalizing the data. Step 2, compute the covariance matrix of this centered data. Step 3, calculate the eigenvectors and eigenvalues of that covariance matrix. Finally, Step 4, map the original data points into the new 'k-dimensional' space by taking linear combinations of the original values using the selected top eigenvectors as weights.

    把这些综合起来看，PCA 是一种将高度相关的、线性相关的特征压缩成少数几个主要的、完全不相关的成分的工具。这方面的一个绝佳应用是在基因组学中。如果你有一个基因表达数据集，其中包含数百名患者，数以千计的单个基因作为特征，你不可能绘制出 10,000 个维度的图。但通过运行 PCA，你可以将这数千个维度映射到仅仅 PC1 和 PC2 两个维度上。当你绘制这两个维度的图时，你可能会清晰地看到患者根据癌症类型聚类，比如纤维腺瘤 (fibroadenoma) 和转移性腺癌 (metastatic adenocarcinoma) 漂亮地分离开来，这纯粹是基于排名前两位的成分所捕获的方差。实现这一目标的算法步骤非常直接：第 1 步，通过减去每个特征的均值来对数据矩阵进行中心化，有效地归一化数据。第 2 步，计算这个中心化数据的协方差矩阵。第 3 步，计算该协方差矩阵的特征向量和特征值。最后，第 4 步，使用选定的顶部特征向量作为权重，对原始值进行线性组合，从而将原始数据点映射到新的‘k 维’空间中。

  - [20:21:44 - 20:27:05] **PCA in Code, Hybrid Models, and Pros/Cons**

    In modern practice, you rarely write these mathematical steps from scratch. It is incredibly straightforward to implement in Python using libraries like scikit-learn. You simply import `PCA` from `sklearn.decomposition`, instantiate the function, fit it to your data, and print the results. Beyond standalone visualization, PCA is heavily used in tandem with other machine learning algorithms. For instance, running K-Means clustering on a 20,000-feature dataset is computationally devastating, and high-dimensional distance calculations are notoriously unreliable. Instead, you run PCA first to compress the data down to 20 highly informative dimensions, and then run K-Means on that embedding. You can do the exact same thing to optimize supervised models like Decision Trees. To wrap up, the main pro of PCA is its ability to elegantly compress and simplify linearly related features. Its fatal flaw, however, is that it is strictly linear. If your original features interact through complex, non-linear relationships, a linear mapping like PCA will fail to capture those patterns effectively, and you will get poor results. In those cases, we need non-linear methods. We are right on time, so since everyone is at home, let's take a 10-minute break and reconvene at 8:36 to discuss t-SNE.

    在现代实践中，你很少需要从头开始编写这些数学步骤。使用像 scikit-learn 这样的 Python 库来实现它是极其简单的。你只需从 `sklearn.decomposition` 导入 `PCA`，实例化该函数，将其拟合到你的数据上，然后打印结果即可。除了独立的视觉化之外，PCA 还被大量地与其他机器学习算法结合使用。例如，在一个拥有 20,000 个特征的数据集上运行 K-Means 聚类在计算上是毁灭性的，而且高维度的距离计算是出了名的不可靠。相反，你会先运行 PCA 将数据压缩到 20 个信息量极高的维度，然后在那个嵌入空间上运行 K-Means。你可以做完全相同的事情来优化像决策树这样的有监督模型。最后总结一下，PCA 的主要优点在于它能优雅地压缩和简化线性相关的特征。然而，它致命的缺陷在于它严格来说是线性的。如果你的原始特征通过复杂的非线性关系相互作用，像 PCA 这样的线性映射将无法有效地捕捉到这些模式，你会得到很差的结果。在这些情况下，我们需要非线性方法。现在时间刚好，既然大家都在家，让我们休息 10 分钟，在 8:36 重新集合，继续讨论 t-SNE。

  - [20:37:19 - 20:39:09] **Introduction to t-SNE**

    Okay, let's go back to the lecture. Earlier, we discussed PCA, which is fundamentally a linear method for dimensionality reduction. Now, we are going to talk about t-SNE, which stands for t-Distributed Stochastic Neighbor Embedding. Unlike PCA, t-SNE is a non-linear method specifically designed for data visualization. It is widely used to visualize high-dimensional data so we can effectively explore underlying patterns, distinct clusters, and complex non-linear relationships. I have provided three primary examples of its application. The first is visualizing the similarities between images in a large dataset. The second example comes from my specific domain: gene expression data analysis, where we use t-SNE very frequently to make sense of complex biological data. The third application is visualizing word embeddings, which are foundational to natural language processing models like ChatGPT and other deep learning approaches.

    好的，我们回到课堂。之前我们讨论了 PCA，它从根本上来说是一种线性的降维方法。现在，我们要讨论 t-SNE，它的全称是 t-Distributed Stochastic Neighbor Embedding (t-分布随机邻域嵌入) 。与 PCA 不同，t-SNE 是一种专门为数据可视化设计的非线性方法 。它被广泛用于可视化高维数据，以便我们能够有效地探索潜在的模式、不同的聚类以及复杂的非线性关系 。我提供了三个主要的应用示例 。第一个是在大型数据集中可视化图像之间的相似性。第二个例子来自我的专业领域：基因表达数据分析，我们非常频繁地使用 t-SNE 来理解复杂的生物学数据 。第三个应用是可视化词嵌入 (word embeddings)，这是像 ChatGPT 这样的自然语言处理模型和其他深度学习方法的基础 。

  - [20:39:09 - 20:44:42] **Visualizing the MNIST Dataset with t-SNE vs PCA**

    Let's look at our first example using an image dataset called the MNIST database. This dataset contains 70,000 grayscale images of handwritten digits ranging from 0 to 9. If you look at the raw data matrix, each row represents a single image of a digit. For instance, the first row might be an image of the digit 5. Each image has a resolution of 28 by 28 pixels. This means if you flatten the image, each row in our dataset has 784 columns (since 28 times 28 is 784), where each column represents a single pixel feature. This is a very popular dataset, and you can easily look up more information about it on Wikipedia. When you look at the raw matrix, you will see a lot of zeros, especially in the first 50 columns, because the borders of these images are typically just empty black space. If you apply t-SNE to visualize this high-dimensional dataset, you get a beautiful 2D plot where each point represents an image, and points with the same color represent images of the same digit. You will see that t-SNE maps the images exceptionally well; images of the same digit are tightly clustered together. For example, images of the digit 8 form a distinct cluster. Interestingly, you might find some images of 9 or 6 clustered slightly closer to the 8s. This is totally reasonable because a hastily written 6 or 9 can look visually similar to an 8, proving that t-SNE accurately captures visual similarity. In contrast, if you use PCA to analyze this exact same dataset, the visualization is not nearly as clean or separated. The main reason is that we are trying to compress over 700 dimensions down to just the first two principal components. Because the mathematical relationships between the pixels forming a digit are highly non-linear, using a linear combination method like PCA results in a massive loss of information. That is why the PCA visualization looks like a blurry, overlapping mess compared to the crisp clusters generated by t-SNE.

    让我们用一个名为 MNIST 数据库的图像数据集来看看我们的第一个例子 。这个数据集包含了 70,000 张从 0 到 9 的手写数字灰度图像 。如果你看原始数据矩阵，每一行代表一张数字图像 。例如，第一行可能是一张数字 5 的图像。每张图像的分辨率是 28 乘 28 像素 。这意味着如果你把图像展平，我们数据集中的每一行都有 784 列（因为 28 乘以 28 是 784），其中每一列代表一个单一的像素特征 。这是一个非常流行的数据集，你可以很容易地在维基百科上查阅到关于它的更多信息 。当你查看原始矩阵时，你会看到很多零，特别是在前 50 列，因为这些图像的边缘通常只是空白的黑色区域。如果你应用 t-SNE 来可视化这个高维数据集，你会得到一个漂亮的 2D 图，其中每个点代表一张图像，相同颜色的点代表相同数字的图像。你会看到 t-SNE 对图像的映射非常好；相同数字的图像被紧密地聚类在一起。例如，数字 8 的图像形成了一个明显的聚类。有趣的是，你可能会发现一些 9 或 6 的图像聚类在稍微靠近 8 的地方。这是完全合理的，因为匆忙写下的 6 或 9 在视觉上可能看起来像 8，这证明 t-SNE 准确地捕捉到了视觉相似性。相反，如果你使用 PCA 来分析完全相同的数据集，其可视化效果远没有这么清晰和分离。主要原因是试图将 700 多个维度压缩到仅仅前两个主成分。由于构成数字的像素之间的数学关系是高度非线性的，使用像 PCA 这样的线性组合方法会导致大量信息丢失。这就是为什么与 t-SNE 生成的清晰聚类相比，PCA 的可视化看起来像是一团模糊重叠的混乱。

  - [20:44:42 - 20:49:18] **Application in Genomics: Bulk vs. Single-Cell RNA Sequencing**

    The second major application is applying t-SNE to gene expression data. There are generally two types of gene expression technologies. The older method is called bulk sequencing. In a bulk sequencing dataset, each row is a feature (a specific gene), and each column is a biological sample, typically a whole chunk of tissue like a cancer biopsy. The problem is that a single piece of tissue contains hundreds of thousands of individual cells of various types. So, the gene expression value you get from bulk sequencing is just a blended, average value across all those different cells, which can be highly misleading. Nowadays, researchers use a much more advanced technology called single-cell RNA sequencing (scRNA-seq). This technology measures gene expression for every single individual cell, providing drastically better biological resolution. In these datasets, we might have over 10,000 features (genes) but only a few hundred cells (data points). If you just look at the raw matrix of gene expression values, it looks like random noise; you cannot see any patterns. However, if you apply t-SNE to this single-cell data, you can clearly map the different cells into distinct, separated clusters. This allows us to classify cells into different biological types based purely on their gene expression profiles. For example, a landmark research paper utilized t-SNE on scRNA-seq data to classify human blood immune cells, specifically monocytes and dendritic cells. By projecting this massive, complex data into 2D via t-SNE, the researchers updated the traditional, original cell classifications and discovered entirely new subtypes of blood cells that were previously invisible. It is a brilliant example of how non-linear dimensionality reduction drives actual scientific discovery.

    第二个主要应用是将 t-SNE 应用于基因表达数据。基因表达技术通常有两种。较老的方法称为批量测序 (bulk sequencing) 。在批量测序数据集中，每一行是一个特征（一个特定的基因），每一列是一个生物样本，通常是一整块组织，比如癌症活检样本 。问题在于，单块组织包含成千上万个各种类型的独立细胞。因此，你从批量测序中得到的基因表达值只是所有这些不同细胞的混合平均值，这可能会产生极大的误导 。如今，研究人员使用一种先进得多的技术，称为单细胞 RNA 测序 (scRNA-seq) 。这项技术能够测量每一个独立细胞的基因表达，提供了大大提升的生物学分辨率。在这些数据集中，我们可能有超过 10,000 个特征（基因），但只有几百个细胞（数据点） 。如果你只看基因表达值的原始矩阵，它看起来就像随机噪声；你根本看不出任何模式。然而，如果你将 t-SNE 应用于这种单细胞数据，你可以清晰地将不同的细胞映射成截然不同、相互分离的聚类 。这使我们能够纯粹基于它们的基因表达谱将细胞分类为不同的生物学类型。例如，一篇里程碑式的研究论文利用 t-SNE 对 scRNA-seq 数据进行降维，对人类血液免疫细胞（特别是单核细胞和树突状细胞）进行了分类 。通过利用 t-SNE 将这种海量、复杂的数据投影到 2D 平面上，研究人员更新了传统的原始细胞分类，并发现了以前无法看到的全血液细胞新亚型 。这是非线性降维如何推动实际科学发现的一个绝佳例子。

  - [20:49:18 - 20:51:44] **Visualizing Word Embeddings**

    Another fantastic application is visualizing word embeddings, which is a crucial concept in Natural Language Processing (NLP). When we train models, we want to map words that have similar semantic meanings into vectors that are physically close to each other in mathematical space. However, these embedding matrices are incredibly high-dimensional. For example, a model like GPT-3 might map a word into an embedding space of 12,288 dimensions across a vocabulary of 50,000 words. It is impossible for humans to directly interpret a 12,000-dimensional matrix to check if the model actually learned semantic relationships. But if we feed that embedding matrix into t-SNE, we get a readable 2D plot. On this plot, you will see that the algorithm successfully maps words with similar meanings to close coordinates. For instance, the point for "Dog" is placed right next to "Cat". "Banana" is clustered near "Apple" and the word "Fruit". Words like "Car" and "Truck" sit together, as do "Man" and "Woman", or "Run" and "Walk". Without non-linear tools like t-SNE, it would be exceptionally difficult to verify or investigate these high-dimensional embeddings.

    另一个极好的应用是可视化词嵌入 (word embeddings)，这是自然语言处理 (NLP) 中的一个核心概念 。当我们训练模型时，我们希望将具有相似语义的词映射到在数学空间中物理上彼此靠近的向量。然而，这些嵌入矩阵是极其高维的。例如，像 GPT-3 这样的模型可能会将包含 50,000 个词的词汇表中的每个词映射到一个 12,288 维的嵌入空间中 。人类是不可能直接解读一个 12,000 维的矩阵来检查模型是否真正学到了语义关系的。但如果我们把这个嵌入矩阵输入到 t-SNE 中，我们就会得到一个易于阅读的 2D 图 。在这张图上，你会看到算法成功地将具有相似含义的词映射到了相近的坐标上。例如，“Dog (狗)”的点就被放置在“Cat (猫)”的旁边 。“Banana (香蕉)”聚集在“Apple (苹果)”和“Fruit (水果)”这个词附近 。像“Car (汽车)”和“Truck (卡车)”这样的词挨在一起，“Man (男人)”和“Woman (女人)”，“Run (跑)”和“Walk (走)”也是如此 。如果没有像 t-SNE 这样的非线性工具，要验证或调查这些高维嵌入将是异常困难的。

  - [20:51:44 - 20:56:56] **The Core Concept of t-SNE: Preserving Local Similarity**

    So, how does this highly popular non-linear dimensionality reduction method actually work? The fundamental key idea is that t-SNE attempts to preserve the local similarity between data points. We mathematically measure this "similarity" using a standard distance function, typically Euclidean distance. The overarching goal is that when we map the data into a low-dimensional visualization (our embedding space), points that were similar (close) in the high-dimensional space are aggressively attracted and placed close together, while dissimilar points are pushed further apart. Let me illustrate this with a simple matrix. Imagine we have five data points in an original 3D space with features X, Y, and Z. We first calculate the pairwise distances between all these points. For instance, the distance between point 1 and point 2 is small, say 0.14. But the distance between point 1 and point 4 is much larger, say 1.00. We compute these distances using the standard squared Euclidean distance formula. Now, imagine we map these points into a new 2D embedding space, and we calculate the pairwise distances in this new space. If the embedding is good, the relative order and scale of these distances should match. A small distance of 0.14 in the high-dimensional space might map to a distance of 0.26 in the low-dimensional space, while the large 1.00 distance maps to something similarly large, like 1.00. The absolute values will be different, but the structural relationship is maintained. t-SNE is essentially designed to iteratively search for an optimal 2D embedding where the pairwise distance matrix of the low-dimensional map is mathematically comparable to the pairwise distance matrix of the original high-dimensional space.

    那么，这种非常受欢迎的非线性降维方法究竟是如何工作的呢？最基本的关键思想是，t-SNE 试图保留数据点之间的局部相似性 。我们在数学上使用标准的距离函数（通常是欧几里得距离）来衡量这种“相似性” 。总的目标是，当我们将数据映射到低维可视化（我们的嵌入空间）时，在高维空间中相似（靠近）的点会被强烈吸引并放置得很近，而不相似的点则会被推得更远 。让我用一个简单的矩阵来说明这一点。假设我们在一个原始的 3D 空间中有五个数据点，特征分别是 X、Y 和 Z 。我们首先计算所有这些点之间的成对距离。例如，点 1 和点 2 之间的距离很小，假设是 0.14。但是点 1 和点 4 之间的距离要大得多，假设是 1.00。我们使用标准的平方欧几里得距离公式来计算这些距离。现在，想象我们将这些点映射到一个新的 2D 嵌入空间中，并且我们在这个新空间中也计算成对距离。如果嵌入效果好，这些距离的相对顺序和比例应该是一致的。在高维空间中 0.14 的小距离可能映射到低维空间中的 0.26，而 1.00 的大距离映射到类似的大数值，比如 1.00。绝对数值会有所不同，但结构关系被维持了下来。t-SNE 本质上被设计为迭代地寻找一个最佳的 2D 嵌入，使得低维映射的成对距离矩阵在数学上与原始高维空间的成对距离矩阵具有可比性。

  - [20:56:56 - 21:05:29] **The t-SNE Algorithm: Probabilities and KL Divergence**

    Let's walk through the specific algorithmic steps. Step one occurs entirely in the original high-dimensional space. We compute the pairwise distances between all points, but then we convert those distances into conditional probabilities using a Gaussian distribution. The formula takes the squared distance between point `i` and point `j`, negates it, divides it by `2 * sigma^2`, and takes the exponential. We then normalize it by dividing by the sum of all other exponentiated distances from point `i`. This gives us `p_j|i`, which is the probability that point `i` would pick point `j` as its neighbor. In this context, `sigma` is controlled by a hyperparameter called perplexity, which roughly equals the number of effective neighbors we want to consider—typically set between 5 and 50. Because distance is symmetric, the raw distance matrix is symmetric, but these conditional probability distributions are not inherently symmetric because the local density (and thus the normalization factor) varies from point to point.

    Step two occurs in our 2-dimensional embedding space. We start with an arbitrary, random 2D scatter of our points. We calculate the pairwise distances between these 2D points, and we convert them into conditional probabilities as well, which we call `q_j|i`. However, instead of a Gaussian distribution, we use a Student's t-distribution with exactly one degree of freedom. The formula here is simpler: `(1 + ||y_i - y_j||^2)^-1`, completely omitting the exponential and the `sigma` parameter. We use the t-distribution in the low-dimensional space to solve the "crowding problem"—it naturally pushes moderately distant points slightly further apart in the 2D visualization to prevent clumps.

    Finally, step three is where the learning happens. We now have two probability matrices: `P` representing the true relationships in the high-dimensional space, and `Q` representing the relationships in our current 2D embedding. If our embedding is good, `P` and `Q` should be nearly identical. To achieve this, t-SNE minimizes a loss function between the two distributions known as the Kullback-Leibler (KL) divergence. Starting from the arbitrary initial embedding, the algorithm uses gradient descent to recursively nudge the positions of the 2D points until the KL divergence loss is minimized, resulting in our final visualization.

    让我们详细了解一下具体的算法步骤。第一步完全发生在原始的高维空间中 。我们计算所有点之间的成对距离，然后使用高斯分布将这些距离转换为条件概率 。该公式取点 `i` 和点 `j` 之间平方距离的负值，除以 `2 * sigma^2`，然后取指数 。接着，我们将其除以点 `i` 到所有其他点的指数化距离的总和来进行归一化。这给了我们 `p_j|i`，即点 `i` 会选择点 `j` 作为其邻居的概率。在这种语境下，`sigma` 由一个称为“困惑度 (perplexity)”的超参数控制，它大致等于我们希望考虑的有效邻居的数量——通常设置在 5 到 50 之间 。因为距离是对称的，原始距离矩阵是对称的，但这些条件概率分布本质上不是对称的，因为局部密度（以及归一化因子）因点而异。

    第二步发生在我们的 2 维嵌入空间中 。我们从数据点的任意、随机的 2D 散点分布开始。我们计算这些 2D 点之间的成对距离，同样将它们转换为条件概率，我们称之为 `q_j|i`。然而，我们在这里使用的不是高斯分布，而是自由度恰好为 1 的学生 t-分布 (Student's t-distribution) 。这里的公式更简单：`(1 + ||y_i - y_j||^2)^-1`，完全省略了指数和 `sigma` 参数 。我们在低维空间中使用 t-分布是为了解决“拥挤问题”——它能自然地在 2D 可视化中将距离中等的点推得稍微远一点，以防止它们挤成一团。

    最后，第三步是实际进行学习的地方。我们现在有两个概率矩阵：代表高维空间中真实关系的 `P`，和代表我们当前 2D 嵌入中关系的 `Q`。如果我们的嵌入效果好，`P` 和 `Q` 应该几乎是相同的。为了实现这一点，t-SNE 最小化了两个分布之间的一种称为 Kullback-Leibler (KL) 散度的损失函数 。从任意的初始嵌入开始，该算法使用梯度下降来递归地微调 2D 点的位置，直到 KL 散度损失降至最低，从而得出我们最终的可视化结果 。

  - [21:05:29 - 21:08:20] **Comparing PCA and t-SNE & Understanding Perplexity**

    Let's directly compare PCA and t-SNE. PCA is a deterministic, linear method focused purely on global dimensionality reduction. It is built strictly on the mathematical eigen-decomposition of a covariance matrix . t-SNE, conversely, is a randomized, non-linear method focused on preserving local structural relationships via k-nearest neighbor embeddings. When I say it is randomized, I mean that the algorithm relies on that initial arbitrary embedding matrix. Every time you run t-SNE, the gradient descent will find a slightly different local minimum, yielding a similar but technically distinct visualization. The hyperparameter for PCA is simply the integer number of principal components you wish to retain. For t-SNE, the primary hyperparameter is perplexity, alongside the learning rate. Perplexity is critical because it explicitly controls the trade-off between prioritizing local similarities versus global similarities. If you set a low perplexity, the algorithm only considers a very tight cluster of immediate neighbors, focusing heavily on local relationships. If you set a high perplexity, it factors in many more neighbors, pulling in global structural relationships. Because of this, t-SNE outputs are notoriously sensitive to the perplexity value chosen.

    让我们直接比较一下 PCA 和 t-SNE 。PCA 是一种确定性的线性方法，纯粹专注于全局降维 。它严格建立在协方差矩阵的数学特征分解之上 。相反，t-SNE 是一种随机的、非线性方法，专注于通过 K 近邻嵌入来保留局部结构关系 。当我说它是随机的时，我的意思是该算法依赖于最初那个任意的嵌入矩阵。每次运行 t-SNE 时，梯度下降都会找到一个略微不同的局部最小值，从而产生一个相似但在技术上截然不同的可视化结果。PCA 的超参数仅仅是你希望保留的主成分的整数个数 。对于 t-SNE，主要的超参数是困惑度 (perplexity)，以及学习率 。困惑度非常关键，因为它明确地控制了优先考虑局部相似性还是全局相似性之间的权衡 。如果你设置了较低的困惑度，算法只会考虑非常紧密的一小圈直接邻居，将重点放在局部关系上 。如果你设置了较高的困惑度，它会把更多的邻居纳入考量，从而引入全局的结构关系 。正因为如此，众所周知，t-SNE 的输出结果对所选的困惑度值极其敏感。

  - [21:08:20 - 21:10:45] **Student Q&A: Correcting a Formula Typo**

    (A student, Tan Yi Chun, raises a question via the voice chat regarding the mathematical formula on slide 41.)

    Student (Tan Yi Chun): "Uh, prof. Is the one that is on slide 41... the conditional probability... because the denominator in the formula, there's only a summation, but there's no exponential sign, but when you work it out, there's a summation of all the exponentials."

    Professor: "You mean this one here? Oh, sorry, there is not missing... Thank you. This is missing the base. The base 'e' is missing here. Thank you for catching that. Let me check the next formula as well. Yes, this one is also missing the base 'e'. Sorry, that is a typo on the slides. The 'e' should be in the denominator inside the summation."

    (The correct formula for the high-dimensional conditional probability uses the exponential function in both the numerator and the denominator, specifically: `p_j|i = e^(-d(i,j)^2 / (2 * sigma^2)) / \Sigma_{k \neq i} e^(-d(i,k)^2 / (2 * sigma^2))` ). I hope that typo doesn't cause too much confusion.

    （一名学生 Tan Yi Chun 通过语音对幻灯片 41 页上的数学公式提出了疑问。）

    学生 (Tan Yi Chun)：“呃，教授。是 41 页幻灯片上的那个……条件概率公式……因为公式的分母里只有一个求和符号，没有指数符号，但当你实际计算时，是对所有的指数进行求和。”

    教授：“你是说这里的这个吗？哦，抱歉，不是缺了……谢谢你。这里漏掉了底数。底数‘e’在这里漏掉了。谢谢你指出这一点。让我检查一下下一个公式。是的，这个也漏掉了底数‘e’。抱歉，那是幻灯片上的一个错字。‘e’应该在分母的求和符号里面。”

    （高维条件概率的正确公式在分子和分母中都使用了指数函数，具体为：`p_j|i = e^(-d(i,j)^2 / (2 * sigma^2)) / \Sigma_{k \neq i} e^(-d(i,k)^2 / (2 * sigma^2))` ）。希望那个错字没有引起太大的困惑。

  - [21:10:45 - 21:12:18] **Visualizing Sensitivity to Perplexity**

    As I was explaining, the t-SNE result is hyper-sensitive to the perplexity value. Imagine we generate 200 random points starting from 4 discrete centers using a Gaussian jump in a 100-dimensional space, meaning we truly have 4 distinct ground-truth clusters. If we run t-SNE with a perplexity of 3 or 5, it breaks up those 4 true clusters into a fragmented mess of tiny sub-clusters, completely distorting the global reality because it is obsessing over local pairs. If we jump to a perplexity of 15, 30, or 50, the algorithm beautifully retrieves and separates the 4 distinct clusters perfectly. However, if we crank the perplexity up to 100, the algorithm considers too many points as neighbors, collapsing the clusters back together into an unreadable, merged shape. You can see this exact same phenomenon when applied to the MNIST dataset. At perplexity equals 5, the digit clusters are shattered into confusing fragments. At a balanced perplexity of 20, the clusters separate wonderfully into logical, distinct colored groups. But at perplexity equals 100, the distinct digit clusters start bleeding into one another, creating a massive, overlapping blob. Finding the "Goldilocks" zone for perplexity is a required step for a successful t-SNE analysis.

    正如我刚才解释的，t-SNE 的结果对困惑度值极其敏感。假设我们在一个 100 维的空间里，从 4 个离散的中心点出发，使用高斯跳跃生成 200 个随机点，这意味着我们在真实情况下确实有 4 个不同的聚类 。如果我们以 3 或 5 的困惑度运行 t-SNE，它会把那 4 个真实的聚类打碎成一堆零碎的小聚类，完全扭曲了全局的真实情况，因为它过于纠结局部的点对关系。如果我们将困惑度调整到 15、30 或 50，算法就能完美地找回并分离开这 4 个截然不同的聚类。然而，如果我们把困惑度提高到 100，算法就会把太多的点视为邻居，从而使得聚类重新坍缩在一起，变成一个难以辨认的混合形状。当你把它应用到 MNIST 数据集时，你能看到完全相同的现象 。当困惑度等于 5 时，数字的聚类被粉碎成了令人困惑的碎片 。在平衡的困惑度 20 下，聚类极好地分离成了合乎逻辑、颜色分明的群体 。但在困惑度等于 100 时，各个数字的聚类开始相互渗透，形成了一个巨大的、重叠的斑块 。为困惑度找到一个“恰到好处”的区间，是成功进行 t-SNE 分析的必经步骤。

  - [21:12:18 - 21:17:53] **Introduction to UMAP and Live Demonstration**

    In summary, we have covered PCA and t-SNE. There is a third modern algorithm similar to t-SNE called UMAP (Uniform Manifold Approximation and Projection). Like t-SNE, UMAP is a non-linear method, but it utilizes mathematical techniques to focus on preserving both the local structure AND the global structure of the data simultaneously. UMAP maps to a weighted graph through k-nearest neighbors. A major practical advantage of UMAP is scalability; it is computationally much faster and works remarkably well on massive datasets where t-SNE might choke. You will frequently see UMAP used heavily in computational biology and scRNA-seq analysis. While PCA and t-SNE are standard tools built into the `scikit-learn` Python library, UMAP is newer and requires installing its own dedicated Python package to call its library. Let me pull up a fantastic interactive website that compares UMAP and t-SNE. Look at this original 3D dataset shaped exactly like an elephant. If we run UMAP and adjust the hyperparameter—specifically the 'neighborhood size', which is UMAP's analog to perplexity—we can manipulate the projection. With a properly tuned neighborhood size, the 2D projection flattens the data while miraculously keeping the global structure intact; it still looks distinctively like a 2D drawing of an elephant. But if we make the parameter too small, the global structure collapses, and the elephant shape is entirely lost, showing how crucial parameter tuning is across all non-linear dimensionality reduction tools.

    总结一下，我们已经涵盖了 PCA 和 t-SNE。还有第三种类似于 t-SNE 的现代算法，叫做 UMAP (Uniform Manifold Approximation and Projection，统一流形近似与投影) 。和 t-SNE 一样，UMAP 也是一种非线性方法，但它利用数学技术来专注于同时保留数据的局部结构和全局结构 。UMAP 通过 k-近邻映射到一个加权图上 。UMAP 在实际应用中的一个主要优势是可扩展性；它的计算速度要快得多，并且在 t-SNE 可能会卡死的海量数据集上表现得异常出色 。你会经常看到 UMAP 在计算生物学和 scRNA-seq 分析中被大量使用 。虽然 PCA 和 t-SNE 是内置在 `scikit-learn` Python 库中的标准工具，但 UMAP 比较新，需要安装它自己专用的 Python 包才能调用其库 。让我打开一个非常棒的交互式网站，它比较了 UMAP 和 t-SNE。看看这个形状完全像大象的原始 3D 数据集。如果我们运行 UMAP 并调整超参数——具体来说是“邻域大小 (neighborhood size)”，相当于 UMAP 里的困惑度——我们可以操纵它的投影 。在适当调整了邻域大小后，2D 投影在将数据扁平化的同时，奇迹般地保持了全局结构的完整性；它看起来仍然像一幅特色鲜明的大象 2D 绘图。但如果我们把参数设得太小，全局结构就会坍塌，大象的形状完全丢失，这表明了在所有非线性降维工具中，参数调整是多么的关键。

  - [21:17:53 - 21:19:07] **Conclusion and Final Project Announcement**

## Week 8
  - [19:07:23 - 19:09:06] **Truncating Negative Values in Linear Models**

    When evaluating our models, we see that in certain regions, the loss is significantly reduced. For instance, if a linear model predicts a negative trading value, we can simply replace that negative prediction with a zero. This truncated value is much closer to the true, real-world value. Whenever we calculate the squared loss—which is the fitted prediction value minus the ground truth value squared—this simple adjustment of enforcing a non-negative sign dramatically improves the model's accuracy. This introduces a non-linear factor to our function. We can apply this trick to various real-world scenarios, such as predicting house sale prices. Suppose we collect data on a house: its size, the number of bedrooms, the location or zip code, and whether it is close to a school or grocery store. A standard linear model uses these five features in the form f_w(x) = b + w_1 x_1 + w_2 x_2 + w_3 x_3 + w_4 x_4 + w_5 x_5. By applying this simple truncation trick to the output, we create a non-linear model that performs considerably better than a strictly linear one.

    在评估我们的模型时，我们发现在某些区域，损失显著降低了。例如，如果线性模型预测出一个负的交易值，我们可以简单地将这个负面预测替换为零。这个截断后的值要比负值更接近真实的客观数值。每当我们计算平方损失（即拟合预测值减去真实值的平方）时，这种强制非负的简单调整就能极大地提高模型的准确性。这就为我们的函数引入了一个非线性因素。我们可以将这个技巧应用于各种现实场景，比如预测房屋销售价格。假设我们收集了一栋房子的数据：它的大小、卧室数量、位置或邮政编码，以及它是否靠近学校或杂货店。标准的线性模型使用这五个特征，形式为 f_w(x) = b + w_1 x_1 + w_2 x_2 + w_3 x_3 + w_4 x_4 + w_5 x_5。通过对输出应用这种简单的截断技巧，我们就能创建一个非线性模型，其表现要比纯线性模型好得多。

  - [19:09:06 - 19:14:33] **The Perceptron and Activation Functions**

    To formalize this, we are essentially using two functions in a row. The first is a standard linear function, which we already understand well. Immediately after that, we apply a second function that forces any negative value to become exactly zero, acting as a hyper-plane boundary. In the positive region, the value remains unchanged, but in the negative region, it becomes a constant zero. This effect is crucial. We calculate the linear function for any data sample to get a raw value, and then we apply this second function to alter the final output. Historically, this concept was first proposed by Frank Rosenblatt 73 years ago, in 1958, as the Perceptron model—a probabilistic model for information storage and organization in the brain. The original Perceptron used a slightly different non-linear function called a binary step activation function, which converts any positive value to 1, and any negative value to 0 (or sometimes -1). We call this second non-linear step the "activation function." It was designed to mimic the biological neurons in our bodies. A biological neuron receives signals from different molecules or surrounding cells. It accumulates these signals, and if the total signal is large enough, it fires—or activates. In our mathematical model, the linear function might output a range of values, say from 3 to -2. The activation function acts as an indicator: if the value is in the positive region, it outputs 1; if it is in the negative region, it outputs 0.

    为了将其公式化，我们实际上是在连续使用两个函数。第一个是标准的线性函数，我们已经非常了解它了。紧接着，我们应用第二个函数，强制任何负值变为确切的零，充当一个超平面边界。在正值区域，数值保持不变；但在负值区域，它变成常数零。这个效果至关重要。我们计算任何数据样本的线性函数以获得一个原始值，然后应用这第二个函数来改变最终输出。从历史上看，这个概念最早由 Frank Rosenblatt 在73年前的1958年提出，称为感知机（Perceptron）模型——一种用于大脑信息存储和组织的概率模型。最初的感知机使用了一种略有不同的非线性函数，称为二元阶跃激活函数（binary step activation function），它将任何正值转换为1，将任何负值转换为0（有时是-1）。我们将这第二个非线性步骤称为“激活函数”。它的设计初衷是为了模仿我们体内的生物神经元。生物神经元接收来自不同分子或周围细胞的信号。它会累积这些信号，如果总信号足够大，它就会触发——或者说激活。在我们的数学模型中，线性函数可能会输出一个范围的值，比如从3到-2。激活函数充当一个指示器：如果该值在正区域，它输出1；如果在负区域，它输出0。

  - [19:14:33 - 19:19:30] **Formalizing the Neural Network Structure**

    Let's look at the formal definition. Suppose our data set has m features. We take the values of feature 1, feature 2, all the way up to feature m. We then apply a linear combination, assigning weights W_1 through W_m to these features, plus one constant bias term, b. If your dataset has m features, your linear model inherently has m + 1 parameters. Receiving these values and applying the linear combination is the first step. The second step is applying the non-linear activation function to output the final value. For a multi-class classification problem, where we want to categorize a data sample into one of K different classes, we cannot just output a single value. Instead, we need K separate linear functions, each outputting a value for one specific class. Mathematically, we represent this efficiently using vector and matrix notation: z = Wx + b. Here, we calculate all K linear functions simultaneously. Then, we apply the activation function point-wise to each of the output values. For example, if our linear vector output is [0.5, 0.3, -0.2], we apply the activation function individually to 0.5, then to 0.3, and then to -0.2. While you could theoretically use a different activation function for each output, in practice, we usually apply the same activation function across all of them.

    让我们看看正式的定义。假设我们的数据集有 m 个特征。我们提取特征1、特征2，一直到特征 m 的值。然后我们应用线性组合，为这些特征分配权重 W_1 到 W_m，加上一个常数偏置项 b。如果你的数据集有 m 个特征，那么你的线性模型本身就包含 m + 1 个参数。接收这些值并应用线性组合是第一步。第二步是应用非线性激活函数来输出最终值。对于多分类问题，我们希望将数据样本分类到 K 个不同的类别之一，我们不能只输出一个单一的值。相反，我们需要 K 个独立的线性函数，每个函数为一个特定类别输出一个值。在数学上，我们使用向量和矩阵表示法高效地表达这一点：z = Wx + b。在这里，我们同时计算所有 K 个线性函数。然后，我们将激活函数逐点（point-wise）应用于每个输出值。例如，如果我们的线性向量输出是 [0.5, 0.3, -0.2]，我们分别对 0.5、0.3 和 -0.2 应用激活函数。虽然理论上你可以为每个输出使用不同的激活函数，但在实践中，我们通常对所有输出应用相同的激活函数。

  - [19:19:30 - 19:28:42] **Exploring Different Activation Functions**

    Why must this second function be non-linear? Because a linear function is fundamentally simple. If you apply multiple linear functions sequentially, the mathematical composition of those linear functions is still just one large linear function. You could stack 100 linear layers, and without non-linearity, it provides no extra mathematical power over a single layer. That is why we rely on simple, non-linear activation functions. The original 1958 paper used the binary step activation. Today, a highly popular choice is ReLU (Rectified Linear Unit), which simply outputs max(z, 0). There is also Leaky ReLU, which is a generalized version designed to catch some of the negative signal. Instead of completely zeroing out a negative value, Leaky ReLU multiplies it by a very small positive factor, alpha (for example, a = 0.1). So, an input of -2 becomes -0.2. This keeps the output closer to zero but preserves a slight gradient. ReLU is actually just a special case of Leaky ReLU where alpha equals zero. Both forms of ReLU produce unbounded outputs on the positive side. Another massive advantage of ReLU is computational efficiency. To train a model using gradient descent, we need to calculate derivatives. The derivative of ReLU is incredibly simple: it is exactly 1 if the input is positive, and 0 if the input is negative. Because calculating this derivative requires almost no computational effort, it massively speeds up the training process. In fact, the famous AlexNet paper noted a 6x speedup during training simply by switching to ReLU from older activation functions.

    为什么这第二个函数必须是非线性的？因为线性函数从根本上来说太简单了。如果你按顺序应用多个线性函数，这些线性函数的数学组合仍然只是一个大的线性函数。你可以堆叠100个线性层，如果没有非线性，它在数学能力上并不比单层更强。这就是为什么我们依赖简单、非线性的激活函数。1958年的原始论文使用了二元阶跃激活。今天，一个非常受欢迎的选择是 ReLU（线性整流单元），它简单地输出 max(z, 0)。还有 Leaky ReLU（带泄露的线性整流单元），这是一个通用版本，旨在捕捉一些负面信号。Leaky ReLU 不是将负值完全归零，而是将其乘以一个非常小的正因子 alpha（例如，a = 0.1）。因此，输入 -2 变成了 -0.2。这使输出更接近于零，但保留了微小的梯度。ReLU 实际上只是 Leaky ReLU 中 alpha 等于零的特例。两种形式的 ReLU 在正半轴上产生的输出都是无界的。ReLU 的另一个巨大优势是计算效率。为了使用梯度下降训练模型，我们需要计算导数。ReLU 的导数异常简单：如果输入为正，导数精确为 1；如果输入为负，导数为 0。由于计算这个导数几乎不需要任何计算量，它极大地加快了训练过程。事实上，著名的 AlexNet 论文指出，仅仅通过从旧的激活函数切换到 ReLU，训练速度就提高了 6 倍。

  - [19:28:42 - 19:35:52] **Sigmoid, Tanh, and Softmax Functions**

    Before ReLU, researchers heavily relied on Tanh and Sigmoid functions. Tanh maps all input values to a tight range between -1 and 1. Sigmoid maps inputs to a range between 0 and 1, which historically represented the firing rate of a neuron. However, both of these suffer from a critical issue called "saturation." If you input a very large positive number or a very large negative number into these functions, the output curve becomes entirely flat. When the curve is flat, the derivative (or gradient) goes to zero. In gradient descent, a zero gradient means the model stops learning entirely because it cannot see how to update the parameters. This saturation problem is a major limitation for deep networks. Finally, for multi-class classification, we use a generalization of the Sigmoid function called Softmax. When your network outputs raw linear scores for different classes—say, e^2 for class one, e^1 for class two, and e^0.1 for class three—these numbers are difficult to interpret. Softmax takes any set of arbitrary positive or negative numbers and mathematically converts them into a rigorous probability distribution. It ensures that every output is bounded between 0 and 1, and crucially, that the sum of all the outputs equals exactly 1. This allows us to interpret the network's output as the percentage confidence for each specific class.

    在 ReLU 之前，研究人员严重依赖 Tanh 和 Sigmoid 函数。Tanh 将所有输入值映射到 -1 和 1 之间的紧凑范围内。Sigmoid 将输入映射到 0 和 1 之间，这在历史上代表了神经元的放电率。然而，这两个函数都面临一个称为“饱和（saturation）”的关键问题。如果你将一个非常大的正数或非常大的负数输入这些函数，输出曲线会变得完全平坦。当曲线平坦时，导数（或梯度）就会趋近于零。在梯度下降中，梯度为零意味着模型完全停止学习，因为它不知道如何更新参数。这种饱和问题是深度网络的一个主要限制。最后，对于多分类问题，我们使用 Sigmoid 函数的推广形式，称为 Softmax。当你的网络为不同类别输出原始线性分数时——比如第一类是 e^2，第二类是 e^1，第三类是 e^0.1——这些数字很难解释。Softmax 接受任何一组任意的正数或负数，并在数学上将它们转换为严格的概率分布。它确保每个输出都在 0 和 1 之间，最关键的是，所有输出的总和精确等于 1。这使我们能够将网络的输出解释为对每个特定类别的百分比置信度。

  - [19:35:52 - 19:42:01] **Training Neural Networks and Gradient Descent**

    Now let's discuss training. Because the neural network model includes these non-linear activation functions, we can no longer solve the problem analytically. There is no simple mathematical formula that will instantly hand us the perfect parameters. Instead, we have to find the best parameters gradually using a multi-step process called Gradient Descent. We define a loss function—such as squared loss or cross-entropy—which compares our model's predicted values against the ground truth. At the very beginning, we just guess the parameters randomly. If you plot the loss function across all possible parameter values, it creates a complex landscape with hills and valleys. Our goal is to find the minimum value, the lowest point in that valley. Because we don't know the landscape beforehand, we calculate the derivative, or the gradient, at our current random point. The calculus tells us the direction of the steepest downward slope. However, knowing the direction isn't enough; we also must decide how far to step. This step size is controlled by a crucial parameter called the "learning rate" (eta). If you choose a learning rate that is too big, your model will literally jump completely over the minimum hole and land on the opposite side of the valley, ruining the progress. If the learning rate is too small, the model will inch forward so slowly that it takes forever to train. Balancing this learning rate requires careful tuning.

    现在我们来讨论训练。因为神经网络模型包含了这些非线性激活函数，我们再也无法通过解析方法（analytically）解决问题了。没有任何简单的数学公式可以立即为我们提供完美的参数。相反，我们必须使用称为梯度下降（Gradient Descent）的多步过程逐步找到最佳参数。我们定义一个损失函数——比如平方损失或交叉熵——它将我们模型的预测值与真实值进行比较。在最开始的时候，我们只是随机猜测参数。如果你将所有可能参数值的损失函数绘制出来，它会形成一个包含山峰和山谷的复杂地形。我们的目标是找到最小值，即那个山谷的最低点。因为我们事先不知道地形，所以我们在当前随机点计算导数或梯度。微积分告诉我们最陡峭的下降斜坡的方向。然而，仅仅知道方向是不够的；我们还必须决定迈出多大的步伐。这个步长由一个称为“学习率（learning rate / eta）”的关键参数控制。如果你选择的学习率太大，你的模型真的会完全跳过最小值的坑，落到山谷的另一边，毁掉之前的进展。如果学习率太小，模型会像蜗牛一样向前爬行，导致训练耗时极长。平衡这个学习率需要仔细的调参。

  - [19:42:01 - 19:51:03] **The XOR Problem and Multi-Layer Networks**

    The true power of neural networks emerged with multi-layer architectures. In 1986, the famous Parallel Distributed Processing (PDP) book popularized the Backpropagation algorithm, which allowed us to successfully train multi-layer models. To demonstrate why a multi-layer network is significantly more powerful than a single-layer one, consider the classic XOR problem. We have a very simple dataset with four points: (0,0) is labeled class 0, (1,0) is class 1, (0,1) is class 1, and (1,1) is class 0. If you plot these on a graph, the positive samples sit at the top-left and bottom-right, while the negative samples are at the bottom-left and top-right. There is absolutely no way you can draw a single straight linear boundary to separate the class 1 points from the class 0 points. A single-layer perceptron entirely fails here. But, if we build a two-layer network, we can solve it. Let's construct a network where the hidden layer calculates two intermediate features: h_1 = g(x_1 + x_2) and h_2 = g(x_1 + x_2 - 1.5), using a standard step activation function g(z). The final output is y = h_1 - h_2. Let's manually test a positive sample where x_1 = 1 and x_2 = 0. For h_1, 1 + 0 = 1, and g(1) = 1. For h_2, 1 + 0 - 1.5 = -0.5, and since it's negative, g(-0.5) = 0. Therefore, the final prediction y = 1 - 0 = 1, which perfectly matches our ground truth! Now let's test a negative sample, (0,0). For h_1, 0 + 0 = 0, and g(0) = 0. For h_2, 0 + 0 - 1.5 = -1.5, giving g(-1.5) = 0. The output y = 0 - 0 = 0, which is exactly right. This proves that by stacking layers and non-linearities, the network can create complex, curved decision boundaries to solve problems that a single layer never could.

    神经网络的真正威力伴随着多层架构的出现而显现。1986年，著名的《并行分布式处理》（PDP）一书普及了反向传播（Backpropagation）算法，使我们能够成功地训练多层模型。为了证明为什么多层网络比单层网络强大得多，考虑经典的 XOR（异或）问题。我们有一个非常简单的数据集，包含四个点：(0,0) 被标记为类别 0，(1,0) 是类别 1，(0,1) 是类别 1，(1,1) 是类别 0。如果你把这些点画在图上，正样本位于左上角和右下角，而负样本位于左下角和右上角。你绝对无法画出一条单一的直线边界来将类别 1 的点与类别 0 的点分开。单层感知机在这里完全失效了。但是，如果我们构建一个两层网络，我们就能解决它。让我们构建一个网络，其隐藏层计算两个中间特征：h_1 = g(x_1 + x_2) 和 h_2 = g(x_1 + x_2 - 1.5)，使用标准的阶跃激活函数 g(z)。最终输出是 y = h_1 - h_2。让我们手动测试一个正样本，其中 x_1 = 1 且 x_2 = 0。对于 h_1，1 + 0 = 1，而 g(1) = 1。对于 h_2，1 + 0 - 1.5 = -0.5，因为它是负数，g(-0.5) = 0。因此，最终预测 y = 1 - 0 = 1，完美匹配了我们的真实值！现在让我们测试一个负样本，(0,0)。对于 h_1，0 + 0 = 0，而 g(0) = 0。对于 h_2，0 + 0 - 1.5 = -1.5，得出 g(-1.5) = 0。输出 y = 0 - 0 = 0，完全正确。这证明了通过堆叠层和非线性，网络可以创建复杂的弯曲决策边界，解决单层网络永远无法解决的问题。

  - [19:51:03 - 19:59:11] **Network Architecture and Parameter Counting**

    When building real-world models, like our earlier house sale price prediction, we can explicitly define hidden layers to capture derived concepts—for example, combining the physical size and number of bedrooms into a "family size capacity" hidden node, and combining location and nearby facilities into a "convenience index" hidden node. However, when we do not possess that prior domain knowledge, we simply build a fully connected neural network and let the machine learn those intermediate representations itself. This means connecting every input feature to every node in the first hidden layer, and so on. A fundamental skill is calculating exactly how many parameters such a network contains. The calculation is straightforward: for any given layer, you multiply the number of input nodes coming into it by the number of neurons in that current layer. This gives you the number of weight parameters. Then, you must add one bias parameter for each neuron in the current layer. So, if an input layer has 6 features and connects to a hidden layer with 3 neurons, you have (6 * 3) weights + 3 biases, resulting in 21 parameters for that connection step alone.
